which are specifically related to kube-apiserver boot-sequences.\n\treturn s.addHealthChecks(0, checks...)\n}\n\n// AddBootSequenceHealthChecks adds health checks to the old healthz endpoint (for backwards compatibility reasons)\n// as well as livez and readyz. The livez grace period is defined by the value of the\n// command-line flag --livez-grace-period; before the grace period elapses, the livez health checks\n// will default to healthy. One may want to set a grace period in order to prevent the kubelet from restarting\n// the kube-apiserver due to long-ish boot sequences. Readyz health checks, on the other hand, have no grace period,\n// since readyz should fail until boot fully completes.\nfunc (s *GenericAPIServer) AddBootSequenceHealthChecks(checks ...healthz.HealthChecker) error {\n\treturn s.addHealthChecks(s.livezGracePeriod, checks...)\n}\n\n// addHealthChecks adds health checks to healthz, livez, and readyz. The delay passed in will set\n// a corresponding grace period on livez.\nfunc (s *GenericAPIServer) addHealthChecks(livezGracePeriod time.Duration, checks ...healthz.HealthChecker) error {\n\tif err := s.healthzRegistry.addHealthChecks(checks...); err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\tif err := s.livezRegistry.addDelayedHealthChecks(livezGracePeriod, checks...); err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\treturn s.readyzRegistry.addHealthChecks(checks...)\n}\n\n// AddReadyzChecks allows you to add a HealthCheck to readyz.\nfunc (s *GenericAPIServer) AddReadyzChecks(checks ...healthz.HealthChecker) error {\n\treturn s.readyzRegistry.addHealthChecks(checks...)\n}\n\n// AddLivezChecks allows you to add a HealthCheck to livez.\nfunc (s *GenericAPIServer) AddLivezChecks(delay time.Duration, checks ...healthz.HealthChecker) error {\n\treturn s.livezRegistry.addDelayedHealthChecks(delay, checks...)\n}\n\n// addReadyzShutdownCheck is a convenience function for adding a readyz shutdown check, so\n// that we can register that the api-server is no longer ready while we attempt to gracefully\n// shutdown.\nfunc (s *GenericAPIServer) addReadyzShutdownCheck(stopCh <-chan struct{}) error {\n\treturn s.AddReadyzChecks(healthz.NewShutdownHealthz(stopCh))\n}\n\n// installHealthz creates the healthz endpoint for this server\nfunc (s *GenericAPIServer) installHealthz() {\n\ts.healthzRegistry.installHandler(s.Handler.NonGoRestfulMux)\n}\n\n// installReadyz creates the readyz endpoint for this server.\nfunc (s *GenericAPIServer) installReadyz() {\n\ts.readyzRegistry.installHandlerWithHealthyFunc(s.Handler.NonGoRestfulMux, func() {\n\t\t// note: installHandlerWithHealthyFunc guarantees that this is called only once\n\t\ts.lifecycleSignals.HasBeenReady.Signal()\n\t})\n}\n\n// installLivez creates the livez endpoint for this server.\nfunc (s *GenericAPIServer) installLivez() {\n\ts.livezRegistry.installHandler(s.Handler.NonGoRestfulMux)\n}\n\n// delayedHealthCheck wraps a health check which will not fail until the explicitly defined delay has elapsed. This\n// is intended for use primarily for livez health checks.\nfunc delayedHealthCheck(check healthz.HealthChecker, clock clock.Clock, delay time.Duration) healthz.HealthChecker {\n\treturn delayedLivezCheck{\n\t\tcheck,\n\t\tclock.Now().Add(delay),\n\t\tclock,\n\t}\n}\n\ntype delayedLivezCheck struct {\n\tcheck      healthz.HealthChecker\n\tstartCheck time.Time\n\tclock      clock.Clock\n}\n\nfunc (c delayedLivezCheck) Name() string {\n\treturn c.check.Name()\n}\n\nfunc (c delayedLivezCheck) Check(req *http.Request) error {\n\tif c.clock.Now().After(c.startCheck) {\n\t\treturn c.check.Check(req)\n\t}\n\treturn nil\n}\n","numLines":168,"startLine":1,"totalLines":168}}}

Architecture:**\\n- `/healthz` - Traditional health endpoint, includes liveness and base health checks\\n- `/livez` - Liveness probe, may have delayed startup grace period\\n- `/readyz` - Readiness probe, indicates full initialization completion\\n- Individual check status available at `/[endpoint]/[check-name]`\\n- Supports exclusion of checks via query parameters: `?exclude=check-name`\\n\\nThe implementation uses a registry pattern where health checks are added during server initialization via `AddHealthChecks()`, `AddBootSequenceHealthChecks()`, `AddReadyzChecks()`, and `AddLivezChecks()` methods.\\n\\n### Grafana/Grafana\\n\\nGrafana implements a simpler health check system focused on operational readiness:\\n\\n**Endpoints:** `/healthz`, `/livez`, `/readyz`, and `/api/health`\\n\\n**Main Implementation Files:**\\n- `pkg/server/health.go` - Core health endpoint handlers\\n- `pkg/api/health.go` - Database health checks\\n- `pkg/api/http_server.go` - HTTP server integration\\n\\n**Health Checks Performed:**\\n1. **Liveness Check** (`/livez`) - Always returns 200 OK via `LivezHandler()`, indicating process is alive\\n2. **Database Health Check** (`/api/health`) - Primary health indicator:\\n   - Executes `SELECT 1` query against the database\\n   - Returns 503 Service Unavailable if database is unreachable\\n   - Caches result for 5 seconds to reduce database load\\n   - Implemented in `pkg/api/health.go` via `databaseHealthy()` function\\n3. **Simple Health Check** (`/healthz`) - Always returns 200 OK, healthNotifier)`\\n\\nThe implementation is more application-aware, checking actual database connectivity rather than internal state synchronization.\\n\\n### Prometheus/Prometheus\\n\\nPrometheus implements a minimal health check system with non-standard endpoint paths:\\n\\n**Endpoints:** `/-/healthy` and `/-/ready` (note the `/-/` prefix instead of `/`)\\n\\n**Main Implementation File:**\\n- `web/web.go` - Web server and endpoint registration\\n\\n**Health Checks Performed:**\\n1. **Healthy Check** (`/-/healthy`):\\n   - Supports both GET and HEAD methods\\n   - Always returns 200 OK with message \\\"[AppName] is Healthy.\\\"\\n   - Indicates the HTTP server is running\\n\\n2. **Ready Check** (`/-/ready`):\\n   - Supports both GET and HEAD methods  \\n   - Returns 200 OK only when `ReadyStatus` equals `Ready`, otherwise 503 Service Unavailable\\n   - Uses `testReady()` wrapper function to check status\\n   - Sets header `X-Prometheus-Stopping: true` if stopping, `false` if not ready\\n   - Returns message \\\"[AppName] is Ready.\\\" on success\\n\\n**Ready Status Management:**\\n- Uses atomic `ReadyStatus` enum with three states: `NotReady`, `Ready`, `Stopping`\\n- Set via `SetReady()` function called during initialization\\n- The `testReady()` function wraps handlers to gate endpoint access based on readiness\\n- No granular health checks like Kubernetes; status is binary\\n\\n**Key Differences:**\\n- Prometheus uses `/-/` prefix convention (common in Prometheus ecosystem)\\n- Simpler implementation without detailed per-component checks\\n- Ready status is application-controlled rather than derived from multiple checks\\n- Provides shutdown state information via response headers\\n\\n### Summary of Differences\\n\\n**Kubernetes** uses a sophisticated check aggregation system where multiple independent components report health status, with support for excluding specific checks. It separately tracks health (general stability), liveness (process alive), and readiness (fully initialized).\\n\\n**Grafana** focuses primarily on database connectivity as the key health indicator, using a simple HealthNotifier flag for readiness state, with database checks cached to reduce load.\\n\\n**Prometheus** implements the simplest approach with binary ready/healthy states controlled by the application itself, using non-standard `/-/` endpoint paths convention and providing shutdown state information in response headers.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":450,"cache_read_input_tokens":53569,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":450},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"d2e32cf3-6b3a-4011-b11d-f84700335bde","uuid":"f7046613-5cdf-4f96-9045-fbc477b243d3"}

Architecture:**\\n- `/healthz` - Traditional health endpoint, includes liveness and base health checks\\n- `/livez` - Liveness probe, may have delayed startup grace period\\n- `/readyz` - Readiness probe, indicates full initialization completion\\n- Individual check status available at `/[endpoint]/[check-name]`\\n- Supports exclusion of checks via query parameters: `?exclude=check-name`\\n\\nThe implementation uses a registry pattern where health checks are added during server initialization via `AddHealthChecks()`, `AddBootSequenceHealthChecks()`, `AddReadyzChecks()`, and `AddLivezChecks()` methods.\\n\\n### Grafana/Grafana\\n\\nGrafana implements a simpler health check system focused on operational readiness:\\n\\n**Endpoints:** `/healthz`, `/livez`, `/readyz`, and `/api/health`\\n\\n**Main Implementation Files:**\\n- `pkg/server/health.go` - Core health endpoint handlers\\n- `pkg/api/health.go` - Database health checks\\n- `pkg/api/http_server.go` - HTTP server integration\\n\\n**Health Checks Performed:**\\n1. **Liveness Check** (`/livez`) - Always returns 200 OK via `LivezHandler()`, indicating process is alive\\n2. **Database Health Check** (`/api/health`) - Primary health indicator:\\n   - Executes `SELECT 1` query against the database\\n   - Returns 503 Service Unavailable if database is unreachable\\n   - Caches result for 5 seconds to reduce database load\\n   - Implemented in `pkg/api/health.go` via `databaseHealthy()` function\\n3. **Simple Health Check** (`/healthz`) - Always returns 200 OK, indicates web server is running\\n4. **Readiness Check** (`/readyz`) - Returns 200 OK only when `HealthNotifier.ready` is true, otherwise 503 Service Unavailable\\n\\n**Readiness Control:**\\n- Uses healthNotifier)`\\n\\nThe implementation is more application-aware, checking actual database connectivity rather than internal state synchronization.\\n\\n### Prometheus/Prometheus\\n\\nPrometheus `web/web.go` - Web server and endpoint registration\\n\\n**Health Checks Performed:**\\n1. **Healthy Check** (`/-/healthy`):\\n   - Supports both GET and HEAD methods\\n   - Always returns 200 OK with message \\\"[AppName] is Healthy.\\\"\\n   - Indicates the HTTP server is running\\n\\n2. **Ready Check** (`/-/ready`):\\n   - Supports both GET and HEAD methods  \\n   - Returns 200 OK only when `ReadyStatus` equals `Ready`, otherwise 503 Service Unavailable\\n   - Uses `testReady()` wrapper function to check status\\n   - Sets header `X-Prometheus-Stopping: true` if stopping, `false` if not ready\\n   - Returns message \\\"[AppName] is Ready.\\\" on success\\n\\n**Ready Status Management:**\\n- Uses atomic `ReadyStatus` enum with three states: `NotReady`, `Ready`, `Stopping`\\n- Set via `SetReady()` function called during initialization\\n- The `testReady()` function wraps handlers to gate endpoint access based on readiness\\n- No granular health checks like Kubernetes; status is binary\\n\\n**Key Differences:**\\n- Prometheus uses `/-/` prefix convention (common in Prometheus ecosystem)\\n- Simpler implementation without detailed per-component checks\\n- Ready status is application-controlled rather than derived from multiple checks\\n- Provides shutdown state information via response headers\\n\\n### Summary of Differences\\n\\n**Kubernetes** uses a sophisticated check aggregation system where multiple independent components report health status, with support for excluding specific checks. It separately tracks health (general stability), liveness (process alive), and readiness (fully initialized).\\n\\n**Grafana** focuses primarily on database connectivity as the key health indicator, using a simple HealthNotifier flag for readiness state, with database checks cached to reduce load.\\n\\n**Prometheus** implements the simplest approach with binary ready/healthy states controlled by the application itself, using non-standard `/-/` endpoint paths convention and providing shutdown state information in response headers.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
